class=\"sharing-clear\"></div></div></div></div><p><iframe src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/208081717?color=ababab&amp;portrait=0\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" frameborder=\"0\" webkitallowfullscreen=\"\" mozallowfullscreen=\"\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/208081717\">The Dream Factory (Director’s Cut)</a> by <a href=\"https://www.rosshaines.com/\">Ross Haines</a> tells the incredible story of the renowned <a href=\"http://www.fendercustomshop.com/\">Fender Custom Shop</a> through the eyes of eight master builders who founded the shop. Each man recounted the emotional ups and downs of the company, the crazy startup environment, and most importantly the pride of craftsmanship. The film was made in conjunction with the 30th anniversary of Fender Custom Shop, for which each of the original luthiers created a “<a href=\"http://www.fendercustomshop.com/features/founders-design/\">Founder’s Design</a>” custom guitar. </p>\n<blockquote><p>The Fender Custom Shop has been called nirvana for guitar lovers. This year marks the 30th anniversary of the legendary shop that’s built guitars for the likes of Eric Clapton, Johnny Cash, Merle Haggard, The Stones, Jimmy Page, Bob Dylan and more. From its inception as a “wild experiment” to current world famous status, this short documentary traces the story using never before seen archival imagery and conversations with the eight original master builders.</p></blockquote>\n<p>via <a href=\"http://airows.com/gear/fender-custom-shop-video\">Airows</a>, <a href=\"http://theawesomer.com/the-dream-factory/420873/\">The wp-image-621137\"></a></p>\n<p>An affectionate <a href=\"https://twitter.com/catpusic\">black and white cat named Pusic</a> joyfully ran to <a href=\"https://youtu.be/DkcCVpEjFPk\">meet his beloved human at the door</a> as he arrived home after being separated for 20 days. Cat Happiness has no limits. Moment of meeting the owner of the cat and after 20 days of separation</em></p>\n<p><iframe width=\"750\" height=\"422\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/DkcCVpEjFPk?rel=0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p>\n<p>In 2014, Pusic was a tiny kitten left for dead in a stairwell. Luckily, he was found by his current human and brought back to full health in a safe home with a couple of affectionate humans who love him very much. </p>\n<p><iframe width=\"750\" height=\"422\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/mHp91SEevwE?rel=0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p>\n<p>Now Pusic’s mission is to pay the kindness forward with <a href=\"https://youtu.be/VyH-oOE_8mA\">lots of hugs</a> and <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/catpusic/\">general cuteness</a>.</p>\n<blockquote><p>Found me in the winter, the sick and the dying. I was saved and cured. Now it’s my turn to save the world from the dark forces and make people happy smile.</p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe width=\"750\" height=\"422\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/VyH-oOE_8mA?rel=0\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-621120\"></a></p>\n<p>Coin engraver <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/user/express375/about\">Shaun Hughes</a> demonstrated the fascinating process by which he transformed a 1973 Lincoln penny profile into a<a href=\"https://youtu.be/klf9hDfRyYE\"> skull with decorative scroll flourishes</a>. This craft, known as <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hobo_nickel\">Hobo Nickel</a>, is  incredibly intricate, but Hughes walks the viewer through every step, making it seem easier than it is.</p>\n<p><iframe width=\"750\" height=\"422\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/klf9hDfRyYE?rel=0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p>\n<p>via <a data-instgrm-payload-id=\"instagram-media-payload-4\" scrolling=\"no\" style=\"background: rgb(255, 255, 255); border: 1px solid rgb(219, 219, 219); margin: 1px 1px 12px; max-width: 750px; width: calc(100% - 2px); border-radius: 4px; box-shadow: none; display: block; padding: 0px;\"></iframe>\n<p><script async=\"\" defer=\"\" src=\"//platform.instagram.com/en_US/embeds.js\"></script></p>\n<p>The <a href=\"https://www.humancharger.com\">HumanCharger</a> is a cleverly designed therapy device that seeks to provide increased energy levels, an improved mood, increased concentration and decreases the effects of jet lag, all with the use of light. Requiring only 12 minutes per day, the HumanCharger directs light through proprietary earphones into photosensitive areas of the brain via the ear canal. The Finnish company <a href=\"https://www.humancharger.com/about/\">Valkee</a> behind the device has <a href=\"https://www.humancharger.com/research/\">studied the ear-brain connection</a> with positive results. The HumanCharger is <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/exec/obidos/ASIN/B00FGUUC34/laughing-squid-20\" data-amzn-asin=\"B00FGUUC34\">available on Amazon</a> in either <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/exec/obidos/ASIN/B00FGUUC34/laughing-squid-20\" data-amzn-asin=\"B00FGUUC34\">black</a> or <a href=\"http://www.amazon.com/exec/obidos/ASIN/B00FGUUCP2/laughing-squid-20\" data-amzn-asin=\"B00FGUUCP2\">silver</a> Amazon. </p>\n<blockquote><p>Recent discoveries have shown that the surface of the brain has photosensitive receptors, much like those located in the retina of the eye. They can be accessed by light flowing through the ear canal using HumanCharger® bright light therapy device and its advanced LEDSet earbuds. When these photosensitive areas of the brain are activated, chemical compounds (Serotonin, Dopamine and Noradrenaline) are released to increase energy levels, improve mood, increase mental alertness and reduce the effects of jet lag.</p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe width=\"750\" height=\"422\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/FdlHz_ZjCIs?rel=0\" frameborder=\"0\" class=\"sharing-clear\"></div></div></div></div><p><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/211519205\"><img src=\"https://laughingsquid.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/sonny-rollins-williamsburg-bridge.gif?w=750\" alt=\"Sonny Rollins Williamsburg Bridge\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-621041\"></a></p>\n<p>In a beautiful episode of “<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLqhIRO8y9HlD5WL0VwXuZJ6b5q8qp9Fac\">Notes from the Ertegun Jazz Hall of Fame</a>“, a collaborative series from <a href=\"http://quotedstudios.org/\">Quoted Studios</a> and <a href=\"http://www.jazz.org\">Jazz at Lincoln Center</a>, an animated version of legendary jazz saxophonist <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonny_Rollins\">Sonny Rollins</a> opened up about his sense of self-confidence, his endless drive to be the best version of himself and that seminal night in 1959 when he went to <a href=\"https://j.gifs.com/8qno7l.gif\">practice his horn on the Williamsburg Bridge</a> during a self-imposed musical sabbatical. This interview took place with journalist <a href=\"http://bensidran.com/\">Ben Sidran</a> on November 14, 1985.  </p>\n<blockquote><p>It was beautiful because you’re playing against the air. You know the sky it was just a beautiful place to practice a horn. It’s a magical thing you know the keys are there on the piano but what you do with them Tuesday night is going to be different than anything you could have thought about Sunday. So this is the magic of it and it’s a beautiful life.\n </p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe src=\"https://player.vimeo.com/video/211519205\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" frameborder=\"0\" webkitallowfullscreen=\"\" mozallowfullscreen=\"\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/211519205\"><img src=\"https://laughingsquid.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/sonny-rollins-bud-powell-miles-davis.gif?w=750\" alt=\"Sonny Rollins Bud Powell Miles Davis\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-621040\"></a></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/211519205\"><img src=\"https://laughingsquid.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/04/sonny-rollins-heart-at-home.gif?w=750\" alt=\"Sonny Rollins Heart at Home\" width=\"750\" height=\"422\" class=\"alignnone size-large wp-image-621044\"></a></p>\n</div></article> <div class=\"between-post-content widget-area\"><div
